## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of a chemical species' concentration as a function of time and current concentration, characteristic of reaction rate laws in chemical kinetics. The explicit dependence on both t and A suggests either a non-elementary rate law or a system with time-dependent parameters.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order decay: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, first-order reactions)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of same species)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (generalized power-law rate law)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic with depletion: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalytic reaction)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Time-modulated rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * t) (linearly time-dependent rate coefficient)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Fractional decay with time: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (power-law coupling of time and concentration)
- Reversible reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (first-order with back-reaction from constant product pool)
- Sigmoidal rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type cooperative kinetics)
- Combined decay and production: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2 (quadratic polynomial rate law)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Mass-action kinetics → Rate proportional to product of reactant concentrations raised to stoichiometric powers: dA_dt ~ A**n
- Enzyme saturation → Rational function of concentration (Michaelis-Menten form) when enzyme-substrate binding limits rate
- Autocatalysis → Product of concentration and remaining capacity: A*(c-A) produces logistic-type behavior
- Cooperative binding → Hill-type terms A**n/(K+A**n) indicate multi-site cooperative mechanisms
- Competing parallel pathways → Sum of power-law terms in concentration: c0*A**n1 + c1*A**n2
- Time-dependent forcing → Explicit t-dependence in rate law suggests external driving (temperature ramp, light modulation, or fed-batch addition)
- Reversible equilibrium → Affine terms in concentration (c0*A + c1) indicate forward and reverse reaction contributions
- Substrate inhibition → Non-monotonic rate vs concentration modeled by A/(c + A**2) or similar rational forms with higher-order denominator

## Analysis

The Ground Truth (GT) is:
`0.79911143444963161*A**0.333333333333333 - 0.49947326957917104*A - 0.49947326957917104*A*exp(-0.050569865727257013*t)`

This has A^(1/3) with a fixed coefficient of 1, but GT needs coefficient 0.79911... ≠ 1. The A^(1/3) term is not multiplied by a free constant, so this doesn't match unless we can absorb it — but we can't since it's hardcoded as 1.

**Candidate 44**: `A**(1/3) + A**3*c0 + A**2*c1 + A*c2 + c3*exp(c4*t) + c5`

Same issue — A^(1/3) has fixed coefficient 1, and there's no `A*exp(t)` term. Also `c3*exp(c4*t)` is not multiplied by A. Doesn't match.

Let me verify **Candidate 36** more carefully:
- `A*c0*exp(c1*t)`: set c0 = -0.49947..., c1 = -0.05057... → matches the third GT term ✓
- `A*c2 + A*c3`: set c2 + c3 = -0.49947... → matches the second GT term ✓

- `c6 + c7*exp(A*c8)`: set c8 = 0, then this becomes c6 + c7. Set c6 = 0, c7 = 0 → vanishes ✓

**Candidate 36 matches the GT.**

Also checking **Candidate 6**: `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + A*c2 + A**c3*c4 + A**c5*c6*exp(c7*t) + c8*exp(A*c9)`

Set c9=0 → c8*1 = c8 (constant). Set c8=0. Set c5 such that the `A**c5*c6*exp(c7*t)` term becomes `A*c6*exp(c7*t)` by setting c5=1. Then we'd have `A*(c0+c6)*exp(...)` but with potentially different exponents c1 vs c7. Actually we need the exp(t) term to be `A*exp(...)`, so set c5=1, c7=c1, then combine. But we also need A^(1/3), so set c3=1/3, c4=0.799... That leaves: `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + A*c2 + A^(1/3)*0.799 + A*c6*exp(c7*t)`. We can combine the two A*exp terms if c1=c7, giving coefficient c0+c6. This works too.

**Candidate 36 is confirmed as a match.**
